*Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Malaysian_general_election*

General elections were held in [[Malaysia]] on Saturday, 19 November 2022.<ref name=":29">{{cite news |last=Ahmad |first=Mohamad Rasdan |date=4 October 2022 |title=Sah PRU Tahun ini |work=[[Kosmo!]] |url=https://www.kosmo.com./2022/10/04/sah-pru-15-tahun-ini/ |access-date=4 October 2022 }}{{Dead link|date=June 2023 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/06/16/dr-m-july-2023-the-best-time-for-ge15|title=Dr M: July 2023 the best date for GE15|website=The Star|date=16 June 2022|access-date=18 July 2022}}</ref> The prospect of [[snap election]]s had been considered high due to the [[2020–2022 Malaysian political crisis|political crisis]] that had been ongoing since 2020; political instability caused by coalition or [[party switching]] among members of Parliament, combined with the fallout of the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Malaysia|COVID-19 pandemic]], contributed to the resignation of two prime ministers and the collapse of each of their respective coalition governments since the [[2018 Malaysian general election|2018 general elections]].

The term of the [[14th Parliament of Malaysia|14th Parliament]] was due to expire on 16 July 2023, five years after its first meeting on 16 July 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.federalgazette.agc.gov.my/outputp/pua_20180613_P.U.%28A%29139.pdf|title=Proclamation – Summon the Parliament [P.U. (A) 139/2018]|publisher=Attorney General's Chamber of Malaysia|date=13 June 2018|access-date=28 February 2020|archive-date=3 January 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200103065938/http://www.federalgazette.agc.gov.my/outputp/pua_20180613_P.U.%28A%29139.pdf|url-status=dead}}</ref> However, the Yang di-Pertuan Agong (King of Malaysia), [[Abdullah of Pahang]], dissolved parliament at the request of Prime Minister [[Ismail Sabri Yaakob]] on 10 October 2022. Constitutionally, the elections were required to be held within 60 days of the dissolution, making 9 December the last possible polling day.<ref name=":3">{{Cite news |date=10 October 2022 |title=Malaysia PM dissolves parliament |language=en |work=Reuters |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/malaysia-pm-dissolves-parliament-2022-10-10/ |access-date=10 October 2022}}</ref>

Historically, general elections for all [[state legislative assemblies of Malaysia]] except [[Sarawak State Legislative Assembly|Sarawak]] had been held concurrently as a cost-saving measure. However, the states could dissolve their own legislatures independently from Parliament, and several states ([[2020 Sabah state election|Sabah]], [[2021 Malacca state election|Malacca]] and [[2022 Johor state election|Johor]]) had held early elections due to the political instability, disrupting their usual electoral cycle. The governments of these states and Sarawak indicated that they would not be holding state elections concurrently. The governments of several other states, primarily those under a [[Pakatan Harapan]] or [[Perikatan Nasional]] government, stated that they would prefer to complete a full term.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.freemalaysiatoday.com/category/nation/2022/06/06/no-early-elections-for-pas-held-states-says-party-vice-president/|title=No early elections for PAS-held states, says party vice-president|date=6 June 2022|access-date=6 June 2022|work=[[Free Malaysia Today]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: Penang, Selangor and Negri not dissolving state assemblies this year, says Anwar |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/05/ge15-penang-selangor-and-negri-not-dissolving-state-assemblies-this-year-says-anwar |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> By 19 October, all Pakatan-led states, [[Penang]], [[Selangor]] and [[Negeri Sembilan]], as well as Perikatan-led states, [[Kedah]], [[Kelantan]] and [[Terengganu]], already confirmed not to be dissolving their state legislatures.<ref name=":7" /><ref name=":8" />

The elections were the first in which 18–20-year-olds were eligible to vote, following a constitutional amendment reducing the [[voting age]] from 21 to 18. Additionally, all voters were automatically [[Voter registration|registered]], so the electorate expanded by around six million people or 31%.<ref>{{Cite news |title=Will young voters in Malaysia revive the career of a 97-year-old politician? |language=en |work=NPR.org |url=https://www.npr.org/2022/11/17/1137334860/will-young-voters-in-malaysia-revive-the-career-of-a-97-year-old-politician |access-date=18 November 2022}}</ref>

Results for 220 out of all 222 contested seats in the Dewan Rakyat were announced by the morning of 20 November 2022, although polling in the constituency of [[Padang Serai (federal constituency)|Padang Serai]] was postponed until 7 December due to the death of the Pakatan Harapan candidate, [[Karuppaiya Muthusamy]], three days before the elections.<ref>{{cite news |date=19 November 2022|title=Padang Serai polls set for dec 7 |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/19/padang-serai-polls-set-for-dec-7 |access-date=20 November 2022}}</ref> Voting in [[Baram (federal constituency)|Baram]] was suspended on polling day due to [[2022 Malaysian east coast floods|flooding and inclement weather]] preventing polling workers from reaching the polling stations, and was instead completed on 21 November.<ref>{{cite news |date=19 November 2022 |title=GE15: Polling for Baram suspended due to bad weather |language=en |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/19/ge15-polling-for-baram-suspended-due-to-bad-weather |access-date=20 November 2022}}</ref>

The elections resulted in a [[hung parliament]], the first federal election to have had such a result in the nation's history. Pakatan Harapan remained the coalition with the most seats in the [[Dewan Rakyat]] albeit with a reduced share, with its largest losses in Kedah. [[Perikatan Nasional]] swept the northwestern and east coastal states of Peninsular Malaysia in a landslide, winning every seat in the states of [[Perlis]], [[Kelantan]] and [[Terengganu]], and all but one in [[Kedah]]; dubbed by many people as the "[[Green Wave (Malaysia)|Green Wave]]" ([[Malay language|Malay]]: "''Gelombang Hijau''").<ref name="Malaysia’s ‘Green Wave’ Was a Long Time Coming">{{cite web|url=https://fulcrum.sg/malaysias-green-wave-was-a-long-time-coming/|title=Malaysia's 'Green Wave' Was a Long Time Coming|work=Fulcrum Singapore|date=26 January 2023 |accessdate=7 March 2023}}</ref><ref name="‘Green wave’ sweeps over voters">{{cite web|url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/12/09/green-wave-sweeps-over-voters|title='Green wave' sweeps over voters|work=The Star|accessdate=7 March 2023}}</ref><ref name="Iman Research: PAS' 'green wave' long time coming, came from lack of Pakatan presence and winning over first-time voters">{{cite web|url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2023/01/20/iman-research-pas-green-wave-long-time-coming-came-from-lack-of-pakatan-presence-and-winning-over-first-time-voters/51161|title=Iman Research: PAS' 'green wave' long time coming, came from lack of Pakatan presence and winning over first-time voters|work=Malay Mail|date=20 January 2023 |accessdate=7 March 2023}}</ref><ref name="‘Gelombang hijau’ PAS akan berkembang dalam PRN, kata Hadi">{{cite web|url=https://www.freemalaysiatoday.com/category/bahasa/tempatan/2023/01/10/gelombang-hijau-pas-akan-berkembang-dalam-prn-kata-hadi/|title='Gelombang hijau' PAS akan berkembang dalam PRN, kata Hadi|work=Free Malaysia Today|accessdate=4 March 2023}}</ref><ref name="ULASAN Kejutan 'Gelombang Hijau' dalam PRU15">{{cite web|url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/646243|title=ULASAN Kejutan 'Gelombang Hijau' dalam PRU15|work=Malaysia Kini|date=30 November 2022 |accessdate=4 March 2023}}</ref><ref name="Bangkitnya 'gelombang hijau' di Malaysia">{{cite web|url=https://www.benarnews.org/malay/komentar/my-abuza-pas-221128-11282022194449.html|title=Bangkitnya 'gelombang hijau' di Malaysia|work=Benar News|accessdate=4 March 2023}}</ref> The historically dominant [[Barisan Nasional]] fell to third place, having lost most of its seats to Perikatan Nasional.

A number of prominent incumbent Members of Parliament lost their seats, including former Prime Minister [[Mahathir Mohamad]] in [[Langkawi (federal constituency)|Langkawi]], where he also forfeited his deposit. Former Finance Minister [[Tengku Razaleigh Hamzah]] was defeated by a narrow margin in [[Gua Musang (federal constituency)|Gua Musang]], while Trade Minister and former Menteri Besar of Selangor, [[Azmin Ali]], lost in [[Gombak (federal constituency)|Gombak]]. Former Housing Minister [[Zuraida Kamaruddin]] was defeated in [[Ampang (federal constituency)|Ampang]], and former Domestic Trade Minister [[Saifuddin Nasution Ismail]] lost in [[Kulim-Bandar Baharu]]. Also defeated were [[Nurul Izzah Anwar]] and [[Mukhriz Mahathir]], the children of Anwar Ibrahim and Mahathir Mohamad, respectively. Former Ministers of the Federal Territories from Barisan Nasional and Pakatan Harapan, [[Tengku Adnan Tengku Mansor]] and [[Khalid Abdul Samad]], were defeated in [[Putrajaya (federal constituency)|Putrajaya]] and [[Titiwangsa (federal constituency)|Titiwangsa]], respectively. Incumbent Finance Minister and Senator [[Tengku Zafrul Aziz]] failed to secure a seat in the Dewan Rakyat for [[Kuala Selangor (federal constituency)|Kuala Selangor]], losing by a narrow margin. Similarly, Health Minister [[Khairy Jamaluddin]], the son-in-law of former Prime Minister [[Abdullah Ahmad Badawi]], was defeated by a slim majority in [[Sungai Buloh (federal constituency)|Sungai Buloh]].

After securing support from Barisan Nasional, [[Gabungan Parti Sarawak]], the [[Heritage Party (Malaysia)|Heritage Party]], [[Malaysian United Democratic Alliance]], [[Parti Bangsa Malaysia]] and several independent MPs,<ref name="motion" /> Pakatan Harapan chairman [[Anwar Ibrahim]] was appointed and sworn in as prime minister on 24 November 2022 by the Yang di-Pertuan Agong.<ref name="PRU15" /><ref name="sworn" /> [[Gabungan Rakyat Sabah]] also expressed its support for Anwar,<ref name="good" /> while Perikatan Nasional opted to assume the role of the official opposition.<ref name="opposition" />

== Background ==
=== Previous election ===
{{Main|2018 Malaysian general election}}
The 2018 federal election resulted in a change in government for the first time in Malaysian history since [[1955 Malayan general election|direct elections were first held in 1955]]. [[Pakatan Harapan]], then a centre-left coalition between four parties, won 113 seats in the [[Dewan Rakyat]] (a two-seat majority) against the right-wing [[Barisan Nasional]] coalition, which won 79 seats. Pakatan Harapan entered government at the federal level with support from the [[Sabah Heritage Party]]. The concurrent state elections also saw Pakatan Harapan winning a majority for the first time in Johor, Malacca and Negeri Sembilan. [[Hung parliament]]s were recorded in Kedah, Perak and Sabah, but changes in party membership of the legislators after the election allowed Pakatan Harapan (or the Sabah Heritage Party in Sabah) to enter government in these states as well.

=== Significant events ===
In July 2019, the ''Constitution (Amendment) Act 2019'', which contained provisions to lower the [[voting age]] to 18 and allow for the automatic [[Voter registration|registration of voters]], was enacted by Parliament.<ref name="The Star">{{cite web|url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2019/07/16/federal-constitution-amended-to-lower-voting-age-to-18/|title=Dewan Rakyat passes Bill to amend Federal Constitution to lower voting age to 18|author1=Martin Carvalho|author2=Hemananthani Sivanandam|author3=Rahimy Rahim|author4=Tarrence Tan|work=The Star|date=16 July 2019|access-date=16 July 2019}}</ref> The [[Election Commission of Malaysia|Election Commission]] announced in June 2020 that preparations for these changes would be ready by July 2021.<ref name="ECvotesat18">{{cite web |title=Kenyataan media – Pendaftaran pengundi 18 tahun |url=https://www.spr.gov.my/sites/default/files/KM%20BIL%2019%20PENDAFTARAN%20PENGUNDI%2018THN.pdf |website=[[Election Commission of Malaysia]] |access-date=13 June 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200613090719/https://www.spr.gov.my/sites/default/files/KM%20BIL%2019%20PENDAFTARAN%20PENGUNDI%2018THN.pdf |archive-date=13 June 2020 |url-status=live |language=ms-MY |date=7 June 2020}}</ref> The 2022 election marked the first in which the 18–20 age group is entitled to vote.<ref name=":25" />

Since losing re-election in 2018, former prime minister [[Najib Razak]] was put on trial, convicted and imprisoned in relation to the [[1MDB scandal]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=Najib in jail: What are his options after losing his final appeal in 1MDB-linked case? |url=https://www.channelnewsasia.com/asia/najib-jail-1mdb-src-international-options-review-application-royal-pardon-2897631 |access-date=26 October 2022 |website=CNA |language=en}}</ref> The scandal severely impacted [[UMNO]] in the previous election and has a continuing legacy in Malaysian politics. Trials and investigations remain ongoing.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Malaysian PM hopes to brush off 1MDB scandal in next election |url=https://asia.nikkei.com/Politics/Malaysian-PM-hopes-to-brush-off-1MDB-scandal-in-next-election |access-date=26 October 2022 |website=Nikkei Asia |language=en-GB}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=23 October 2022 |title='Still angry': as Malaysians lose faith in politics, will new faces offer hope? |url=https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/politics/article/3196764/malaysians-still-angry-over-2018-election-set-vote-amid-political-strife-rocky-economy |access-date=5 November 2022 |website=South China Morning Post |language=en}}</ref>

The [[COVID-19 pandemic in Malaysia]] emerged as a major health crisis from early 2020.  It had significant impacts on Malaysia's [[Economic impact of the COVID-19 pandemic in Malaysia|economy]] and [[Social impact of the COVID-19 pandemic in Malaysia|society]].<ref>{{Cite web |date=12 January 2021 |title=Malaysia declares Covid state of emergency amid political turmoil |url=http://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/jan/12/malaysia-declares-covid-state-of-emergency-amid-political-turmoil |access-date=11 October 2022 |website=The Guardian |language=en}}</ref><ref name=":2" />

=== 2020–22 political crisis ===
{{Main|2020–2022 Malaysian political crisis}}

A [[2020–2022 Malaysian political crisis|political crisis]] began in Malaysia in early 2020, leading to the resignation of two prime ministers and significant shifts in parliament over the subsequent two years.<ref name=":2">{{Cite news |last1=Chu |first1=Mei Mei |last2=Latiff |first2=Rozanna |last3=Lee |first3=Liz |date=16 August 2021 |title=Malaysian PM Muhyiddin resigns as political crisis escalates |language=en |work=Reuters |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/malaysian-pm-expected-resign-after-months-political-turmoil-2021-08-16/ |access-date=11 October 2022}}</ref> In late February 2020, a majority of the 32 members of the [[Malaysian United Indigenous Party]] withdrew from the governing [[Pakatan Harapan]]-led coalition, causing it to lose its majority in the Dewan Rakyat, and partnered with [[Barisan Nasional]]. Prime Minister [[Mahathir Mohamad]] then resigned, creating a [[power vacuum]] in the executive branch.<ref name=":1">{{Cite web |date=16 August 2021 |title=A timeline of events leading to Malaysian PM's resignation |url=https://apnews.com/article/health-coronavirus-pandemic-malaysia-44d7b29132368c47cc87a90f72daf8a6 |access-date=11 October 2022 |website=AP NEWS |language=en}}</ref> This movement later became known as ''Sheraton Move.'' On 1 March, [[Muhyiddin Yassin]] was appointed prime minister, and a Malaysian United Indigenous Party-led [[Muhyiddin cabinet|minority government]] was formed under new coalition [[Perikatan Nasional]], with [[confidence and supply]] from Barisan Nasional.<ref name=":1" /> Political instability continued after this, [[Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on politics in Malaysia|exacerbated by the impact]] of the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Malaysia|COVID-19 pandemic]]. The crisis escalated in mid-2021, leading to Muhyiddin losing parliamentary support over the COVID-19 response and resigning.<ref name=":2" /> On 20 August 2021, [[Ismail Sabri Yaakob]] was appointed prime minister as his replacement.<ref>{{Cite web |date=20 August 2021 |title=Malaysia appoints third prime minister in as many years |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/asia/southeast-asia/ismail-sabri-yaakob-malaysia-pm-b1905862.html |access-date=11 October 2022 |website=The Independent |language=en}}</ref>

This political instability led to calls for a [[Snap election|snap general election]] from various lawmakers, and there was speculation that one would be held since 2020.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Teoh |first1=Shannon |date=12 June 2020 |title=Malaysia PM Muhyiddin Yassin looks to snap polls to end battle with predecessor Mahathir |language=en-SG |work=[[The Straits Times]] |url=https://www.straitstimes.com/asia/se-asia/malaysia-pm-muhyiddin-yassin-looks-to-snap-polls-to-end-battle-with-predecessor |url-access=subscription |access-date=13 June 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Soo |first1=Wern Jun |date=12 June 2020 |title=Report: Snap polls talk gains momentum in Malaysia |language=en-MY |work=[[Malay Mail]] |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2020/06/12/report-snap-polls-talk-gains-momentum-in-malaysia/1874832 |url-status=live |access-date=13 June 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200613062305/https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2020/06/12/report-snap-polls-talk-gains-momentum-in-malaysia/1874832 |archive-date=13 June 2020}}</ref><ref name=":4">{{Cite news |last=Shukry |first=Anisah |date=1 June 2022 |title=Malaysia PM Says Won't Delay Dissolving Parliament Once Ready |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2022-06-01/malaysia-pm-says-won-t-delay-dissolving-parliament-once-ready |access-date=30 June 2022}}</ref> In June 2022, Ismail Sabri said he would not delay the dissolution of parliament, amid continued pressure from his party [[United Malays National Organisation|UMNO]] to hold a general election as soon as possible. He said he would consult with his allies in the [[Barisan Nasional]] alliance on the date, as well as leaders of his party [[United Malays National Organisation|UMNO]].<ref name=":4" /> Ismail Sabri announced the dissolution on 10 October 2022.<ref name=":3" />

== Electoral system ==
{{Further|Elections in Malaysia}}
[[Elections in Malaysia]] are conducted at the federal and state levels. Federal elections elect members of the [[Dewan Rakyat]], the lower house of [[Parliament of Malaysia|Parliament]], while state elections in each of the 13 states elect members of their respective [[State legislative assemblies of Malaysia|state legislative assembly]]. As Malaysia follows the [[Westminster system]] of government, the [[head of government]] ([[Prime Minister of Malaysia|Prime Minister]] at the federal level and the [[Chief Ministers in Malaysia|Chief Ministers]], the so-called {{Em|Menteri Besar}}, at the state level) is the person who commands the confidence of the majority of members in the respective legislature – this is normally the leader of the party or coalition with the majority of seats in the legislature.

The Dewan Rakyat consists of 222 members, known as Members of Parliament (MPs), that are elected for five-year terms. Each MP is elected from a [[single-member district|single-member constituency]] using the [[first-past-the-post voting|first-past-the-post voting system]]. If one party obtains a majority of seats, then that party is entitled to form the government, with its leader becoming the prime minister. In the event of a [[hung parliament]], where no single party obtains the majority of seats, the government may still form through a [[coalition]] or a [[confidence and supply]] agreement with other parties. In practice, coalitions and alliances in Malaysia generally persist between elections, and member parties do not normally contest for the same seats.

In July 2019, the ''Constitution (Amendment) Act 2019'' was enacted that provided for the voting age to be lowered to 18 and for automatic registration of voters.<ref name="The Star" /> Previously, the [[voting age]] was 21<ref>{{cite web|url=http://says.com/my/news/how-to-register-as-a-voter-in-malaysia|title=Here's The Fastest Way To Register As A Voter Before The Next Elections|author=Nandini Balakrishnan|publisher=Says.com|date=28 September 2016|access-date=9 May 2018|quote=Qualifications needed to register as a voter in Malaysia:<br />a) A Malaysian citizen above the age of 21.<br />b) A resident of an [[List of Malaysian electoral districts|election constituency]].<br />c) Is not disqualified by any laws.}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://juiceonline.com/a-young-malaysians-guide-to-the-election/|title=A Young Malaysian's Guide to the Election|publisher=Juice|date=30 March 2018|access-date=9 May 2018|quote=You are not eligible to register if you are:<br />a) on the qualifying date, you are serving jail term or detained as a person of [[mental disorder|unsound mind]].<br />b) before the qualifying date, you have been convicted or [[Capital punishment in Malaysia|sentenced to death]] or serving a jail term of more than 12 months and you're still liable on the qualifying date.<br />c) found guilty under the Election Offences Act, 1954.<br />d) have a foreign citizenship (Malaysian citizenship law does not permit a Malaysian to carry [[dual citizenship]]).}}</ref> although the [[age of majority]] in the country was 18.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.commonlii.org/my/legis/consol_act/aoma1971153/|title=Age of Majority Act 1971|publisher=The Commissioner of Law Revision, Malaysia|date=22 April 1971|access-date=9 May 2018}}</ref> Automatic [[voter registration]] and the lowered voting age simultaneously came into effect in early 2022, with this election being the first federal election with the expanded electoral franchise.<ref name="ECvotesat18" /> Malaysia does not currently practice [[compulsory voting]]. The Election Commission is under the jurisdiction of the [[Prime Minister's Department (Malaysia)|Prime Minister's Department]].

In late 2022, several news outlets and publishing companies began launching apps and websites to announce the upcoming GE15 results and news.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Here are the best apps to get Malaysia's general elections (GE15) Polling Results and News |url=https://beamstart.com/news/malaysia-ge15-results-app |access-date=7 October 2022 |website=Here are the best apps to get Malaysia's general elections (GE15) Polling Results and News |language=en}}</ref>

== Timeline ==
=== Dissolution of parliament ===
The 14th Parliament of Malaysia was dissolved on 10 October 2022, during a special televised address by Prime Minister [[Ismail Sabri Yaakob]], following an audience with the Yang di-Pertuan Agong, Abdullah, a day prior, whereby he provided consent for the dissolution. The election had to be held within 60 days or by 9 December.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Zahiid |first=Syed Jamal |date=10 October 2022 |title=PM Ismail Sabri dissolves Parliament to pave way for GE15 |work=[[Malay Mail]] |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/10/pm-ismail-sabri-dissolves-parliament-to-pave-way-for-ge15/32746 |access-date=10 October 2022}}</ref>

The [[Constitution of Malaysia]] requires that a general election be held in the fifth calendar year after the first sitting unless it is dissolved earlier by the [[Yang di-Pertuan Agong]] following a [[motion of no confidence]], [[loss of supply]] or a request by the [[Prime Minister of Malaysia|prime minister]].

=== Dissolution of state legislatures ===
While any state may dissolve its legislature independently of Parliament, most of them had historically dissolve at around the same time as Parliament such that federal and state elections are held simultaneously. In accordance with Malaysian law, [[Parliament of Malaysia|Parliament]] as well as the [[State legislative assemblies of Malaysia|legislative assemblies of each state]] would automatically expire on the fifth anniversary of the first sitting of a term, unless dissolved prior to that date by the relevant [[State governments of Malaysia#Heads of state|heads of state]] on the advice of their respective [[Chief Ministers in Malaysia|heads of government]]. Elections must be held within sixty days of expiry or dissolution.

=== Pre-nomination events ===
On 17 October 2022, the Election Commission of Malaysia (SPR) updated the roster of 63 parties and coalitions eligible to contest in its own right. Independents are allowed to contest using symbols predefined by the SPR.<ref>{{Cite web |title=SIMBOL PARTI YANG BERDAFTAR DENGAN SPR SEHINGGA 17 OKTOBER 2022 |url=https://www.spr.gov.my/sites/default/files/SIMBOL%20PARTI%20YANG%20BERDAFTAR%20DENGAN%20SPR%20SEHINGGA%2017%20OKTOBER%202022.pdf |publisher=Election Commission of Malaysia |access-date=23 October 2022 |archive-date=22 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221022133824/https://www.spr.gov.my/sites/default/files/SIMBOL%20PARTI%20YANG%20BERDAFTAR%20DENGAN%20SPR%20SEHINGGA%2017%20OKTOBER%202022.pdf |url-status=dead }}</ref>

== Last election pendulum ==
(Results and status at 9 May 2018) The 14th general election witnessed 124 governmental seats and 98 non-governmental seats filled the [[Dewan Rakyat]]. The government side has 49 safe seats and 11 fairly safe seats, while the other side has 21 safe seats and 4 fairly safe seats.{{collapse top|}}

== Political parties and candidates==
{{Main|List of candidates in the 2022 Malaysian general election}}

The election saw numerous changes in seats from all political sides, with candidates either announced to be departing from their original constituencies to contest in another constituency, or several high-profile members of parliament being dropped from selection. Those who were dropped or not selected however went on to contest as [[Independent politician|independent candidates]] or in opposing parties to defend their seats or seek re-election, resulting in their memberships dropped.

UMNO deputy president [[Mohamad Hasan (politician)|Mohamad Hasan]] announced his intention to contest the [[Rembau (federal constituency)|Rembau seat]], replacing incumbent [[Khairy Jamaluddin]], who was expected to be fielded in an opposition-majority seat,<ref>{{Cite web |last=Zulkifli|first=Syamilah |date=16 October 2022 |title=Tok Mat mampu menang besar di Rembau: Khairy |url=https://www.sinarharian.com.my/article/226209/berita/politik/tok-mat-mampu-menang-besar-di-rembau-khairy |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=Sinar Harian |language=ms}}</ref> which eventually turned out to be [[Sungai Buloh (federal constituency)|Sungai Buloh]], one of the seats that has been a PKR stronghold.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Yeong |first=Ashley |date=1 November 2022 |title=BN confirms Khairy for Sungai Buloh in GE15 to loud cheers |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/11/01/bn-confirms-khairy-for-sungai-buloh-in-ge15-to-loud-cheers/36878 |access-date=1 November 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref> In addition, several high-profile incumbent UMNO MPs, including [[Shahidan Kassim]], [[Annuar Musa]] and [[Tajuddin Abdul Rahman]], were dropped from contesting following rumors after they were believed to be supporting Ismail Sabri instead of Zahid Hamidi.<ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: Four ministers among big guns likely dropped from contesting |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/31/ge15-four-ministers-among-big-guns-likely-dropped-from-contesting |access-date=2 November 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref><ref name=":12" /> Among those dropped, [[Zahidi Zainul Abidin]], the incumbent [[Padang Besar (federal constituency)|Padang Besar]] MP, contested as an independent while Shahidan contested to defend his [[Arau (federal constituency)|Arau seat]] under the Perikatan banner, resulting in both their and several others' memberships dropped.<ref>{{Cite web |date=7 November 2022 |title=Shahidan, Zahidi, Ismail and Azhar expelled from Umno – Ahmad Maslan |url=http://www.theedgemarkets.com/article/shahidan-zahidi-ismail-and-azhar-expelled-umno-%E2%80%94-ahmad-maslan |access-date=16 November 2022 |website=The Edge Markets |archive-date=16 November 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221116141800/https://www.theedgemarkets.com/article/shahidan-zahidi-ismail-and-azhar-expelled-umno-%E2%80%94-ahmad-maslan |url-status=dead }}</ref> In a similar move, incumbent PAS [[Tumpat (federal constituency)|Tumpat]] MP [[Che Abdullah Mat Nawi]] contested to defend his seat under the BN ticket after he was dropped from the candidates' list, resulting in him expelled from PAS.<ref>{{Cite web |title=PAS leaders contesting under different banner are automatically expelled, says Hadi |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/04/pas-leaders-contesting-under-different-banner-are-automatically-expelled-says-hadi |access-date=16 November 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref>

A few of the more notable changes in PKR were Anwar's decision to contest in the [[Tambun (federal constituency)|Tambun parliamentary seat]],<ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: Anwar to contest in Tambun parliamentary seat |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/20/ge15-anwar-to-contest-in-tambun-parliamentary-seat |access-date=30 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> with [[Wan Azizah Wan Ismail]] contesting the [[Bandar Tun Razak (federal constituency)|Bandar Tun Razak seat]], as part of PKR's plan to field high-ranking members in seats previously held by defected party members.<ref>{{Cite web |date=23 September 2022 |title=PKR likely to field big guns against 'pengkhianat', says Anwar |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/636738 |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> One of the most anticipated seats, [[Gombak (federal constituency)|Gombak]], saw Selangor's Menteri Besar [[Amirudin Shari]] nominated as PH candidate to face incumbent [[Azmin Ali]],<ref>{{Cite web |author1=Ng Xiang Yi |author2=Alena Nadia |date=28 October 2022 |title=Selangor MB Amirudin to take on Azmin in Gombak, others dropped |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/641505 |access-date=30 October 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> who was one of the key ringleaders of [[2020–2022 Malaysian political crisis|the ongoing political crisis]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=PKR announces its candidates for GE15 |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/28/pkr-announces-its-candidates-for-ge15 |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> PKR also announced several other high-profile direct candidates to contest under the PH banner.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Razak |first=Radzi |date=26 October 2022 |title=Nik Aziz's son among seven key community leaders announced as PKR's GE15 candidates |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/26/nik-azizs-son-among-seven-key-community-leaders-announced-as-pkrs-ge15-candidates/35704 |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref> Former [[Batu (Kuala Lumpur federal constituency)|Batu]] MP [[Tian Chua]], who was not selected to contest in favor of incumbent [[Prabakaran Parameswaran]], sought to seek re-election by contesting as an independent candidate for his seat, leading to his expulsion from the party.<ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: Tian Chua to be sacked from PKR for running as an independent, says Anwar |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/05/ge15-tian-chua-to-be-sacked-from-pkr-for-running-as-an-independent-says-anwar |access-date=16 November 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref>

Meanwhile, DAP had dropped two of its incumbent MPs, [[Charles Santiago]] and [[Wong Tack]] from their respective parliamentary seats,<ref>{{Cite web |title=Charles Santiago dropped in Klang |url=https://www.thesundaily.my/local/charles-santiago-dropped-in-klang-DF10041507 |access-date=29 October 2022 |newspaper=The Sun |location=Malaysia |language=en-MY}}</ref> in place of younger candidates,<ref>{{Cite web |last=Jun |first=Soo Wern |date=26 October 2022 |title=GE15: Loke confirms Wong Tack out, Young Syefura in for Bentong contest |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/26/ge15-loke-confirms-wong-tack-out-young-syefura-in-for-bentong-contest/35660 |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=26 October 2022 |title=DAP drops Santiago, Kota Kemuning rep Ganabatirau to stand in Klang |url=https://www.thevibes.com/articles/news/75326/dap-drops-santiago-kota-kemuning-rep-ganabatirau-to-stand-in-klang |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=The Vibes |language=en}}</ref> leading both to question the party's reasoning behind their droppings,<ref>{{Cite web |title=Dropped duo fire salvos at DAP |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/29/dropped-duo-fire-salvos-at-dap |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> with Wong later announcing his intention to defend his seat as an independent candidate,<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ong |first=Justin |date=26 October 2022 |title=Dropped in Bentong, Wong Tack goes solo to take on DAP's Rara |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/26/dropped-in-bentong-wong-tack-goes-solo-to-take-on-daps-rara/35722 |access-date=29 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref> thus also resulting in his expulsion from the party.<ref>{{Cite web |title=以独立人士上阵文冬 黄德被开除党籍！ – 全国大选 – 最新消息 |url=https://www.sinchew.com.my/20221106/%e4%bb%a5%e7%8b%ac%e7%ab%8b%e4%ba%ba%e5%a3%ab%e4%b8%8a%e9%98%b5%e6%96%87%e5%86%ac-%e9%bb%84%e5%be%b7%e8%a2%ab%e5%bc%80%e9%99%a4%e5%85%9a%e7%b1%8d%ef%bc%81/ |access-date=16 November 2022 |website=星洲网 Sin Chew Daily Malaysia Latest News and Headlines |language=zh-Hans}}</ref>

On 16 November, [[Padang Serai (federal constituency)|Padang Serai]]'s incumbent MP [[Karupaiya Mutusami]] died three days before the election.<ref name=":28" /> This marked the third time in Malaysian election history that a nominated candidate died in between nomination and polling dates.<ref>{{Cite web |date=16 November 2022 |title=GE15: Padang Serai ballot likely to be delayed |url=https://www.thevibes.com/articles/news/77510/ge15-padang-serai-ballot-likely-to-be-delayed |access-date=16 November 2022 |website=The Vibes |language=en}}</ref> The Election Commission announced that polling for Padang Serai would take place on 7 December following a meeting on Friday (18 November),<ref>{{Cite web |last=Tong |first=Geraldine |date=18 November 2022 |title=EC postpones Padang Serai polling to Dec 7 |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/644785 |access-date=18 November 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> a day before the elections,<ref>{{Cite web |date=16 November 2022 |title=EC to meet on Friday to fix date for Padang Serai contest |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/644481 |access-date=16 November 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> after polling for the constituency was postponed.<ref>{{Cite web |date=17 November 2022 |title=Election in Padang Serai postponed following candidate's death |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/644678 |access-date=17 November 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> Subsequently, PN candidate for the [[Tioman (state constituency)|Tioman state seat]] in Pahang, Yunus Ramli died hours before polling was due to begin on 19 November.<ref>{{Cite web |title=PN's Tioman candidate Yunus Ramli passes away |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/19/pn039s-tioman-candidate-yunus-ramli-passes-away |access-date=19 November 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> The election for the state seat was also postponed to the same date with Padang Serai.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Election in Tioman: EC sets Nomination Day on Nov 24, polling on Dec 7 |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/19/election-in-tioman-ec-sets-nomination-day-on-nov-24-polling-on-dec-7 |access-date=19 November 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref>

=== Parties represented in current legislatures ===
The election would be the first time Pakatan Harapan, Gabungan Parti Sarawak, Gabungan Rakyat Sabah and Perikatan Nasional use their own respective logos.

DAP announced their intention to use the PH logo for West Malaysia seats on 14 November 2021,<ref>{{Cite web |title=DAP to use Pakatan logo for GE15 in peninsula, Sabah and Sarawak branches free to decide |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2021/11/14/dap-to-use-pakatan-logo-for-ge14-in-peninsula-sabah-and-sarawak-branches-fr/2020781 |access-date=16 December 2021 |website=Malay Mail |date= 14 November 2021|language=en}}</ref> while they would continue to use their own logo in Sarawak as they did in the previous election and also in the recent state election.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Sulok |first=Tawie |date=13 October 2022 |title=GE15: Sarawak PKR, Amanah to use Pakatan logo; DAP inclined to use 'Rocket' symbol |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/13/ge15-sarawak-pkr-amanah-to-use-pakatan-logo-dap-inclined-to-use-rocket-symbol/33429 |access-date=18 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=23 October 2022 |title=GE15: Sarawak DAP will use its rocket logo |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/640800 |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> However, DAP stated that they would be joining other PH parties in using the PH logo in Sabah, in contrast to using their own logo in the previous election, the [[2019 Sandakan by-election]] and using then-ally Warisan's logo in the [[2020 Sabah state election]].<ref>{{Cite news |date=23 October 2022 |title=Unlike Sarawak, we're not using rocket logo for GE15: Sabah DAP |url=https://www.thevibes.com/articles/news/75056/unlike-sarawak-were-not-using-rocket-logo-for-ge15-sabah-dap |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=The Vibes |language=en}}</ref> In September 2022, Pakatan formally decided to consider applications by [[Malaysian United Democratic Alliance|MUDA]] and the [[Socialist Party of Malaysia]] (PSM) to contest under its name.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Selvam |first=Kousalya |date=22 September 2022 |title=Muda, PSM's desire to work with PH to be looked into, assures Adam Adli |url=https://www.sinardaily.my/article/180446/malaysia/national/muda-psms-desire-to-work-with-ph-to-be-looked-into-assures-adam-adli |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=Sinar Daily |language=en}}</ref> Pakatan chairman [[Anwar Ibrahim]] later stated that the coalition would form an [[electoral pact]] with the two parties, citing that the application process would need to go through the Registrar of Societies.<ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: Pakatan will form electoral pact with Muda, says Anwar |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/12/ge15-pakatan-will-form-electoral-pact-with-muda-says-anwar |access-date=18 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> However, on 30 October, PSM announced that they ended their pact with PH, after they were denied being allocated seats for the election, in particular [[Sungai Siput (federal constituency)|Sungai Siput]] where chairman [[Michael Jeyakumar Devaraj]] served two terms but was similarly allocated to PKR in 2018.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ong |first=Justin |date=30 October 2022 |title=PSM ends pact with Pakatan after allegedly given no seat for GE15 |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/30/psm-ends-pact-with-pakatan-after-allegedly-given-no-seat-for-ge15/36421 |access-date=30 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref> Therefore, PSM decided to contest alone on 2 November 2022

PN component parties in Pahang (Bersatu, PAS, Gerakan) decided to contest on all parliamentary and state assembly seats there on 28 November 2021.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Perikatan Nasional to contest in all 14 parliament, 42 state seats in Pahang in GE15 |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2021/11/28/perikatan-nasional-to-contest-in-all-14-parliament-42-state-seats-in-pahang-in-ge15 |access-date=16 December 2021 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> The [[Malaysian Islamic Party]] (PAS), despite being in the PN coalition, announced that they would be contesting using their own logo in Kelantan, Terengganu and Kedah along with other PN candidates in these three predominant Malay/Muslim states.<ref>{{Cite web |date=14 October 2022 |title=PAS to use own logo in Kelantan, Terengganu and Kedah |url=https://www.freemalaysiatoday.com/category/nation/2022/10/14/pas-to-use-own-logo-in-kelantan-terengganu-and-kedah/ |access-date=18 October 2022 |website=Free Malaysia Today}}</ref> The move was met with objection from GERAKAN, as their policy was to not contest under other party's logo.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Gerakan will not use PAS logo in GE15 |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/18/gerakan-will-not-use-pas-logo-in-ge15 |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> Some of PN component parties are also part of Gabungan Rakyat Sabah, who intended to use GRS logo in Sabah.<ref>{{Cite web |date=12 October 2022 |title=GE15: Bersatu candidates in Sabah to contest under GRS logo – Muhyiddin |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/639210 |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> Parti Kesejahteraan Demokratik Masyarakat ([[Social Democratic Harmony Party|KDM]]), a GRS-friendly party initiated by former Warisan Party members, sought to contest at least three seats in Sabah independently.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Sabah's Parti KDM to go solo in GE15 |url=https://www.theborneopost.com/2022/10/21/parti-kdm-to-go-solo-in-ge15/ |access-date=22 October 2022 |website=The Borneo Post |date=21 October 2022 |language=en-US}}</ref>

In August 2022, Pejuang formed a Malay/Muslim-based coalition called as [[Gerakan Tanah Air]] (GTA) with 4 other parties (Berjasa, Putra, Gagasan Bangsa and IMAN) and planned to contest 120 parliamentary seats.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Dr M's Gerakan Tanah Air eyes 120 seats in GE15 |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/08/04/dr-ms-gerakan-tanah-air-eyes-120-seats-in-ge15 |access-date=7 August 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> Mahathir, who initially hesitated to contest until he changed his mind to defend his [[Langkawi (federal constituency)|Langkawi seat]], announced that GTA would be contesting under the Pejuang logo, while GTA contestants in Kelantan contested using the logo of [[Parti Bumiputera Perkasa Malaysia]] (PUTRA), as the coalition's registration was still pending.<ref>{{Cite web |date=11 October 2022 |title=Mahathir will defend Langkawi seat in Malaysia GE {{!}} The Straits Times |url=https://www.straitstimes.com/asia/se-asia/mahathir-will-defend-langkawi-seat-in-malaysia-ge |access-date=18 October 2022 |website=The Straits Times |language=en}}</ref>

Barisan Nasional contested all parliamentary seats outside Sarawak,<ref>{{Cite web |date=16 October 2022 |title=BN tanding 191 kerusi |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/639839 |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref> while respecting Sabah state liaison office's intention to cooperate with Gabungan Rakyat Sabah.<ref>{{Cite web |date=15 October 2022 |title=GE15: Close to 50–50 seats split between GRS, BN in Sabah |url=https://www.malaysiakini.com/news/639709 |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=Malaysiakini}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=23 October 2022 |title=Ismail Sabri: BN-GRS cooperation vital to ensure joint victory in GE15 |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/23/ismail-sabri-bn-grs-cooperation-vital-to-ensure-joint-victory-in-ge15/35187 |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref> On 11 December 2021, PBRS announced that they would contest 3 seats in Sabah under Barisan Nasional.<ref>{{Cite web |title=PBRS to contest in Penampang, Moyog, Kepayan |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2021/12/11/pbrs-to-contest-in-penampang-moyog-kepayan/2027759 |access-date=16 December 2021 |website=Malay Mail |date= 11 December 2021|language=en}}</ref> In April 2022, UMNO's Supreme Council proposed that Prime Minister Ismail Sabri Yaakob be its Prime Ministerial candidate for GE15.<ref>{{Cite web |date=14 April 2022 |title=Umno proposes Ismail Sabri Yaakob as its candidate for PM at next general election |url=https://www.straitstimes.com/asia/se-asia/umno-proposes-ismail-sabri-as-its-candidate-for-pm-at-next-general-election |access-date=24 April 2022 |website=The Straits Times |language=en}}</ref> Zahid Hamidi, chairman of Barisan Nasional, has officially considered to accept [[Malaysia Makkal Sakti Party|Makkal Sakti]]'s request to contest the election under Barisan Nasional logo on 19 September 2021.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Nasir |first=Aslinda |date=19 September 2021 |title=Makkal Sakti diberi tempat pada PRU-15 – Ahmad Zahid |url=https://www.utusan.com.my/terkini/2021/09/makkal-sakti-diberi-tempat-pada-pru-15-ahmad-zahid/ |access-date=30 January 2022 |website=Utusan Digital |language=ms-MY}}</ref> The offer was extended to other Friends of BN parties by June 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2 June 2022 |title='Friends of BN' almost certain of becoming BN candidates in GE15 – Zahid |url=http://www.theedgemarkets.com/article/friends-bn-almost-certain-becoming-bn-candidates-ge15-%E2%80%94-zahid |access-date=27 August 2022 |website=The Edge Markets |archive-date=28 November 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221128054517/https://www.theedgemarkets.com/article/friends-bn-almost-certain-becoming-bn-candidates-ge15-%E2%80%94-zahid |url-status=dead }}</ref> Gabungan Parti Sarawak, whose component parties were part of BN in 2018 election, formulated its election program and competed independently. GPS postponed any coalition and government formation talks until after election and claimed to maintain the status quo of seat allocation.<ref>{{Cite web |date=14 September 2022 |title=Seat distribution: GPS maintains status quo, says Abang Jo |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/09/13/seat-distribution-gps-maintains-status-quo-says-abang-jo/28112 |access-date=28 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref>

In this election, the Heritage Party (WARISAN), previously an ally of Pakatan Harapan in the 2018 general election, for the first time contested outside Sabah. As part of the move, it intended on 24 January 2021 to contest all parliamentary and assembly seats in Penang and considered to run in other states.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Warisan to contest all seats in Penang in GE15 |url=https://www.msn.com/en-my/news/national/warisan-to-contest-all-seats-in-penang-in-ge15/ar-AAT4BSS?ocid=BingNewsSearch |access-date=24 January 2022 |publisher=MSN}}</ref>

=== Extra-parliamentary parties ===
On 15 December 2021, a group of independent activists calling themselves Gerak Independent announced their intention to run in the election in no more than 10 seats.<ref>{{Cite web |date=16 December 2021 |title=Not here to play: Siti Kasim to make political debut in GE15 |url=https://www.thevibes.com/articles/news/49811/not-here-to-play-the-fool-siti-kasim-to-make-political-debut-in-ge15 |access-date=16 December 2021 |website=The Vibes |language=en}}</ref> [[Parti Bumi Kenyalang]] (PBK) initially intended to contest all 31 parliamentary seats in Sarawak on 26 January 2022, claiming that it already made ties with unspecified Sabah based party and still opened possibility of cooperating with other Sarawak-only parties.<ref>{{Cite web |date=26 January 2022 |title=PBK to contest all 31 parliamentary seats in S'wak |url=https://www.thevibes.com/articles/news/52984/pbk-to-contest-all-31-parliamentary-seats-in-swak |access-date=26 January 2022 |website=The Vibes |language=en}}</ref> By June 2022 PBK made negotiations with Sarawakian local opposition parties such as PSB, [[Parti Aspirasi Rakyat Sarawak|Aspirasi]], [[Parti Bansa Dayak Sarawak Baru|PBDS (Baru)]] and SEDAR to avoid clashes in the election without formally forming a coalition.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Sarawak based opposition parties to meet on seat allocation this month |url=https://www.theborneopost.com/2022/06/04/sarawak-based-opposition-parties-to-meet-on-seat-allocation-this-month/ |access-date=7 August 2022 |website=The Borneo Post |date=4 June 2022 |language=en-US}}</ref> The negotiation produced a cooperation pact between PSB, PBK and PBDS, with PBK contesting mostly under PSB's logo.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2 October 2022 |title=PSB, PBK and PBDS formalise collaboration for GE15 |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/02/psb-pbk-and-pbds-formalise-collaboration-for-ge15/31175 |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: PBK to field four candidates as of now, says Voon |url=https://www.theborneopost.com/2022/10/22/pbk-to-field-four-candidates-as-of-now-says-voon/ |access-date=22 October 2022 |website=The Borneo Post |date=22 October 2022 |language=en-US}}</ref> In June 2022 SEDAR announced their intention to contest in Malay/Muslim (and Melanau)-majority of Sarawak seats.<ref>{{Cite web |title=PRU15: SEDAR sah bertanding, sasar lapan kerusi majoriti Melayu-Melanau |url=https://www.astroawani.com/berita-politik/pru15-sedar-sah-bertanding-sasar-lapan-kerusi-majoriti-melayumelanau-369507 |access-date=18 October 2022 |website=[[Astro Awani]] |language=Malay}}</ref>

[[Parti Rakyat Malaysia]] announced their intention to contest parliamentary seats in Penang respectively on 15 October 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |title=PRM jumps into the election fray, contesting five Parliamentary seats in Penang |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/15/prm-jumps-into-the-election-fray-contesting-five-parliamentary-seats-in-penang |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> PRM later stated that it would contest 28 parliament and 1 state seats nationally, in cooperation with GERAK 98 NGO.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ismail |first=Rohana |date=22 October 2022 |title=PRU15: PRM bertanding di semua kerusi Parlimen di Kelantan |url=https://www.utusan.com.my/nasional/2022/10/pru15-prm-bertanding-di-semua-kerusi-parlimen-di-kelantan/ |access-date=22 October 2022 |website=Utusan Malaysia |language=ms-MY}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last1=Yakkub |first1=Mohd Yunus |date=1 November 2022 |title=PRU15: PRM umum tanding 28 Parlimen, 1 DUN |url=https://www.kosmo.com.my/2022/11/01/pru15-prm-umum-tanding-28-parlimen-1-dun/ |access-date=1 November 2022 |website=Kosmo Digital |language=ms-MY}}</ref>

Parti Cinta Sabah, Penang Front Party and Sarawak People's Aspiration Party initially declared to their intention to participate but ended up not fielding any candidates.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Asmin |first=Asyikin |date=1 November 2022 |title=Anifah bakal bertanding di Kimanis? |url=https://www.sinarharian.com.my/article/228635/berita/politik/anifah-bakal-bertanding-di-kimanis |access-date=1 November 2022 |website=Sinar Harian |language=ms}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Aspirasi not fielding anyone in Sibu, Lanang, Bintulu and Miri |url=https://www.theborneopost.com/2022/10/22/aspirasi-not-fielding-anyone-in-sibu-lanang-bintulu-and-miri/ |access-date=22 October 2022 |website=The Borneo Post |date=22 October 2022 |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=17 June 2022 |title=Penang Front Party plans to contest in 10 state and parliamentary seats, says its chairman |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/06/17/penang-front-party-plans-to-contest-in-10-state-and-parliamentary-seats-says-its-chairman/12857 |access-date=18 October 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref>

=== Nominated candidates ===
The election saw a record 945 candidates contesting in all 222 parliamentary seats nationwide, among them a record 108 independent candidates.<ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15 in numbers |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/11/06/ge15-in-numbers |access-date=6 November 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> {{collapse top|}}

|[[Mahfuz Omar]]
| bgcolor="{{Pakatan Harapan/meta/shading}}" |'''PH (AMANAH)'''
|Noran Zamini Jamaluddin
| bgcolor="{{United Malays National Organisation/meta/shading}}" |'''UMNO'''

== Campaign ==
=== Timing of election ===
Opposition politicians, political analysts and online commentaries criticised the decision to hold the election at the end of 2022 instead of early 2023, which coincides the annual year-end [[monsoon]] season.<ref>{{Cite web |date=19 September 2022 |title=Will you take blame for lost lives if GE held during floods, MP asks Zahid |url=https://www.freemalaysiatoday.com/category/nation/2022/09/19/will-you-take-blame-for-lost-lives-if-ge-held-during-floods-mp-asks-zahid/ |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=Free Malaysia Today}}</ref><ref name=":9">{{Cite web |last=Hassan |first=Hakem |date=19 September 2022 |title="We will proceed" – Zahid Hamidi Slammed For Harshly Saying Elections Must Go On Despite Floods |url=https://worldofbuzz.com/we-will-proceed-zahid-hamidi-slammed-for-harshly-saying-that-elections-must-go-on-despite-floods/ |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=worldofbuzz.com |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=30 September 2022 |title=Year-end not the right time for GE15, say experts |url=https://www.malaysianow.com/news/2022/09/30/year-end-not-the-right-time-for-ge15-say-experts |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=MalaysiaNow |language=en}}</ref> As Malaysia was already recovering from [[2021–2022 Malaysian floods|serious flooding from the previous year]], opposition politicians accused the ruling government for being inconsiderate towards flood victims. This condition was also seen by opposition parties as a deliberate tactic to discourage a high [[voter turnout]] that could potentially benefit opposition parties.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2 October 2022 |title=Low voter turnout due to floods will help Umno win GE15 |url=https://www.malaysia-today.net/2022/10/02/low-voter-turnout-due-to-floods-will-help-umno-win-ge15/ |access-date=28 October 2022 |website=Malaysia Today |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Osman |first=Hamzah |date=17 October 2022 |title=Umno taking advantage of floods to win GE15, says Dr Mahathir |url=https://www.nst.com.my/news/politics/2022/10/841321/umno-taking-advantage-floods-win-ge15-says-dr-mahathir |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=New Straits Times}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Hassan |first=Hakem |date=16 October 2022 |title=DAP Politician Says Govt Purposely Chose to Have GE During Floods in Hopes of Lower Voter Turn-Out |url=https://worldofbuzz.com/dap-politician-says-govt-purposely-chose-to-have-ge-during-floods-in-hopes-of-lower-voter-turn-out/ |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=worldofbuzz.com |language=en-US}}</ref> In response, UMNO president [[Ahmad Zahid Hamidi]], who remarked that the election was to proceed despite concerns of nationwide floods,<ref name=":9" /> accused opposition parties as "cowards" and "wanting them to buy time" to garner extra support, further adding that his remarks were taken out of context.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Zahid says his comment on floods and GE15 taken out of context |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/09/21/zahid-says-his-comment-on-floods-and-ge15-taken-out-of-context |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=27 September 2022 |title=Ahmad Zahid: Opposition are running scared of GE15, trying to buy time with flood, inflation narrative {{!}} Daily Express Online – Sabah's Leading News Portal |url=http://www.dailyexpress.com.my/news/199996/ahmad-zahid-opposition-are-running-scared-of-ge15-trying-to-buy-time-with-flood-inflation-narrative/ |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=www.dailyexpress.com.my}}</ref> Despite these remarks, authorities began preparations in the event flooding occurs during polling day.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Zainuddin |first=Faiz |date=12 October 2022 |title=Police resources will be stretched if it floods during GE15 |url=https://www.freemalaysiatoday.com/category/nation/2022/10/12/police-resources-will-be-stretched-if-it-floods-during-ge15/ |access-date=28 October 2022 |website=Free Malaysia Today}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=GE15: 'Over and above' preparations made in facing floods, says Hishammuddin |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2022/10/16/ge15-over-and-above-preparations-made-in-facing-floods-says-hishammuddin |access-date=28 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref>

The decision to dissolve parliament early was also seen by several other opposition politicians as an attempt to prevent more BN politicians from being charged with [[Corruption in Malaysia|corruption]], or in an effort towards pardoning jailed politicians such as former prime minister [[Najib Razak]] who was found guilty for his role in the [[1MDB scandal]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Pei Ying |first=Teoh |date=12 October 2022 |title=Kit Siang: GE15 is to save Umno and BN "Court Clusters" |url=https://www.nst.com.my/news/politics/2022/10/839745/kit-siang-ge15-save-umno-and-bn-court-clusters |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=New Straits Times}}</ref> This was evidenced by a video online showing Zahid Hamidi speaking at a [[Malaysian Indian Congress]] (MIC) general meeting in which he warned other BN politicians that they would be the next ones to be charged should BN lose the election.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Ram |first=Sadho |date=12 October 2022 |title=Zahid Hamidi Warns More BN Politicians Will Face Corruption Charges If Party Loses GE15 |url=https://says.com/my/news/zahid-hamidi-warns-more-bn-politicians-will-face-corruption-charges-if-bn-loses-ge15 |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=SAYS}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Alena |date=12 October 2022 |title="If we lose, we'll all get charged" – M'sians Are Upset After Hearing Zahid Hamidi's Speech About GE15 |url=https://worldofbuzz.com/if-we-lose-well-all-get-charged-msians-areupset-after-hearing-zahid-hamidis-speech-about-ge15/ |access-date=24 October 2022 |website=worldofbuzz.com |language=en-US}}</ref> Prime Minister Ismail Sabri Yaakob said he dissolved Parliament because it was impossible to go on some issues, and that UMNO was pushing for it ever since BN won big in the [[2022 Johor state election]] in March.<ref>{{Cite web |date=13 October 2022 |title=PM Ismail Sabri denies dissolving Parliament after pressure from Umno |url=https://www.malaymail.com/news/malaysia/2022/10/13/pm-ismail-sabri-denies-dissolving-parliament-after-pressure-from-umno/33376 |access-date=10 November 2022 |website=Malay Mail |language=en}}</ref>

=== Youth vote ===
The 2022 election was the first Malaysian federal election in which the voting age is over 18 as opposed to over 21 previously. Around 6 million new voters, either young or previously unregistered, were expected to participate in the election.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Margues |first=Clara Ferreira |date=18 October 2022 |title=Will Malaysia's Young Voters Use Their Power? |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/opinion/articles/2022-10-17/will-malaysia-s-young-voters-use-their-power-in-the-upcoming-election}}</ref> The 18–20 age group represented 1.39 million first-time voters, and voters aged 18–39 account for about 50% of Malaysia's 21 million registered voters.<ref name=":25">{{Cite news |last1=Sipalan |first1=Joseph |last2=Azmi |first2=Hadi |date=28 October 2022 |title=Malaysia election: As race heats up to win youth vote, do veteran MPs pass the 'vibe check'? |work=[[South China Morning Post]] |url=https://www.scmp.com/week-asia/politics/article/3197475/malaysia-election-race-heats-win-youth-vote-do-veteran-mps-pass-vibe-check}}</ref>

== Endorsements ==
{{Main|Endorsements in the 2022 Malaysian general election}}

Newspapers, organisations and individuals endorsed parties or individual candidates for the election.

== Outgoing members of parliament ==
The seats of [[Gerik (federal constituency)|Gerik]] and [[Batu Sapi (federal constituency)|Batu Sapi]] were left vacant due to the deaths of their respective MPs, [[Hasbullah Osman]] (BN-UMNO) and [[Liew Vui Keong]] (WARISAN) in 2020.<ref name=":30">{{Cite web |title=Gerik MP Hasbullah dies (updated) |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2020/11/16/gerik-mp-hasbullah-dies |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref><ref name=":31">{{Cite web |title=Batu Sapi MP Liew Vui Keong dies |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/news/nation/2020/10/02/batu-sapi-mp-liew-vui-keong-dies |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=The Star |language=en}}</ref> By-elections were due to be held, but did not materialise due to [[2021 Malaysian state of emergency|the declaration of the state of emergency]] during the [[COVID-19 pandemic]] in 2021.<ref>{{Cite news |date=12 January 2021 |title=Malaysia declares Covid state of emergency amid political challenges |language=en-GB |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/55625448 |access-date=16 October 2022}}</ref> The declarations were later revoked by the [[Yang di-Pertuan Agong]] following the dissolution of parliament.<ref>{{Cite web |date=7 October 2022 |title=King revokes emergency proclamations for Gerik, Batu Sapi and Bugaya |url=https://www.freemalaysiatoday.com/category/nation/2022/10/07/king-revokes-emergency-proclamations-for-gerik-batu-sapi-and-bugaya/ |access-date=16 October 2022 |website=Free Malaysia Today}}</ref>
